## Top of Mind Cracks in private credit

PDF Summary - Top of Mind Cracks in private credit

Source file:
- 1. Top of Mind_ Cracks in private credit.pdf
Pages in representative file: 27
Readable text extracted from grouped file(s): 278,900 characters

Duplicate/logical-duplicate handling: this draft summarizes the following selected variants once:
- 1. Top of Mind_ Cracks in private credit.pdf
- 2.Top of Mind_ Cracks in private credit.pdf

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, oil-market supply risk and inflation transmission, rates, duration, and term-premium repricing, credit positioning and private-credit risk, consumer demand, pricing, and category mix. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- After over a decade of rapid growth and relative calm, private credit has come under pressure as high-profile defaults, concerns about inflated valuations, and substantial exposure to a software industry vulnerable to AI disruption have fueled a surge in redemption requests.
- Could these stresses trigger a systemic crisis?
- And even if not, could they dampen the outlook for private credit?
- Oaktree's Howard Marks, Ares' Michael Arougheti, Marathon's Bruce Richards, and GS' Amanda Lynam agree current private credit stresses don't pose systemic risk.
- But they somewhat disagree on private credit's near-to-medium term outlook.

Key data and arguments
- Datapoints/trends we're focused on â€¢ Iran war; even with sufficient oil reserves, we think Japan faces potentially significant indirect oil supply constraints as shortages abroad impact global supply chains. â€¢ BoJ policy; we continue to expect the next rate hike in July, though uncertainty about the timing remains high. â€¢ Shunto spring wage negotiations show a marginally softer base pay rise from 2025, but still high in the mid-3% range. â€¢ Japanese consumer confidence, which deteriorated sharply.
- Latest GS proprietary datapoints/major changes in views â€¢ We lowered our 2026 Japan real GDP growth forecast to 0.3% (from 0.4%) and raised our 2027 core CPI forecast to 2.3% (from 2.1%) given the higher oil prices we now expect.
- Howard Marks: To avoid managers having to sell assets at unrealistically low prices that would be injurious to their investors and potentially to their business, private credit vehicles are designed either to prohibit investors from taking back their capital, as is the case with traded BDCs, or to allow them to take back only a certain percentage-typically 5% of NAV- per quarter, as is the case with non-traded BDCs.
- Europe Emerging Markets (EM) Latest GS proprietary datapoints/major changes in views â€¢ We raised our 1Q26 UK GDP growth forecast after better- than-expected February GDP data, bringing our full-year 2026 growth forecast to 1.0% (Q4/Q4, vs.
- Datapoints/trends we're focused on â€¢ Iran war; we think the impact of the current energy price shock on European manufacturing should be notably smaller and less persistent than the 2022/23 energy crisis. â€¢ ECB policy; we expect the ECB to hike rates in June and September but view whether the ECB hikes twice or remains on hold this year as a close call. â€¢ UK employment growth, which remains weak.
- Latest GS proprietary datapoints/major changes in views â€¢ We raised our 2026/27 China PPI forecasts to 1.2%/0.9% (from 1%/0.6%) given the higher oil prices we now expect.
- Arougheti and Lynam aren't particularly worried about software exposure and expect credit fundamentals to remain healthy as long as the economy holds up, while Richards is more concerned about software risk and sees a painful default cycle ahead.
- Michael Arougheti 3% of the HY bond market is software loans versus 13% of the broadly syndicated loan market and a whopping 23% of the private credit market...
- Datapoints/trends we're focused on â€¢ Iran war; longer energy supply disruptions that result in even higher gasoline prices would likely lead to a larger drag on consumer spending. â€¢ Fed Chair transition; we don't expect a major reduction in the Fed's balance sheet under Kevin Warsh as Fed Chair. â€¢ US labor market, which we expect to soften this year due to weaker growth, higher energy costs, and modestly greater reluctance to hire for jobs that can be done by AI.
- Euro area: a less painful energy shock than 2022 Monthly change in price-related surveys, std. dev.
- He points out that 23% of the private credit market is software loans, which he says is an excessive figure by any standard, with leverage at the fund level and especially the company level further magnifying the risk from this exposure.
- For example, should a loan be valued at its "fundamental value"-which is hard to estimate-or at the price an investor could sell it for today, or at the price they could get a month from now after prospective buyers have had the opportunity to conduct due diligence, or at the price an investor would have to pay to buy an equivalent loan?
- Bruce Richards: I expect incredibly high software sector default rates in 2027, 2028, and 2029, with peak defaults of 15% and double-digit default rates in each of those years given the valuation reset this year and likely reluctance of the broadly syndicated loan and direct lending markets to extend new credit to highly leveraged, below-investment grade software companies.
- After over a decade of rapid growth and relative calm, private credit has come under pressure as high-profile defaults, concerns about inflated valuations, and substantial exposure to a software industry vulnerable to AI disruption have fueled a surge in redemption requests.

Risks, catalysts, and watch points
- Oaktree's Howard Marks, Ares' Michael Arougheti, Marathon's Bruce Richards, and GS' Amanda Lynam agree current private credit stresses don't pose systemic risk.
- Arougheti and Lynam aren't particularly worried about software exposure and expect credit fundamentals to remain healthy as long as the economy holds up, while Richards is more concerned about software risk and sees a painful default cycle ahead.
- So, it's hard to argue that there isn't too much software risk in direct lending.
- Datapoints/trends we're focused on â€¢ Iran war; longer energy supply disruptions that result in even higher gasoline prices would likely lead to a larger drag on consumer spending. â€¢ Fed Chair transition; we don't expect a major reduction in the Fed's balance sheet under Kevin Warsh as Fed Chair. â€¢ US labor market, which we expect to soften this year due to weaker growth, higher energy costs, and modestly greater reluctance to hire for jobs that can be done by AI.
- Datapoints/trends we're focused on â€¢ Iran war; even with sufficient oil reserves, we think Japan faces potentially significant indirect oil supply constraints as shortages abroad impact global supply chains. â€¢ BoJ policy; we continue to expect the next rate hike in July, though uncertainty about the timing remains high. â€¢ Shunto spring wage negotiations show a marginally softer base pay rise from 2025, but still high in the mid-3% range. â€¢ Japanese consumer confidence, which deteriorated sharply.
- We ask several long-time industry watchers for their perspectives: Howard Marks, Co-Founder and Co-Chairman of Oaktree Capital Management, Michael Arougheti, Co-Founder and CEO of Ares Management, Bruce Richards, CEO, Chairman, and Co-Founder of Marathon Asset Management, and Amanda Lynam, GS Chief Credit Strategist.

Investment advice or portfolio implication
- No explicit single-security investment rating was detected in the extracted text; treat the document as macro/sector context unless the original PDF contains a recommendation outside the extract.

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, consumer demand, pricing, and category mix, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk, gold positioning and real-rate/geopolitical hedges. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- Agentic AI has burst onto the evolving AI scene with significant promise, capturing the imagination of industry practitioners and investors alike.
- At its fullest, Agentic AI can handle a wide range of tasks currently done by humans in a fully autonomous way.
- On the other hand, Agentic AI could be misdirected and counterproductive, consuming vast resources with little return.
- In this report, we outline some of the likely use cases we see for Agentic AI across the enterprise and consumer sphere - and quantify potential upside to business outcomes, along with the investment levels required.
- Moving past concepts to numbers: We see Agentic AI driving a dramatic increase in token consumption of 24X or 120 quadrillion tokens per month by 2030.

Key data and arguments
- Investment Implications For hyperscalers and model providers, we prefer the following stocks (covered n by Eric Sheridan): AMZN (Buy, $325 12-m PT): We continue to see visibility into returns as AWS o revenues compound, supported by a reported $364bn revenue backlog, driven by both AI workloads and rising momentum around its custom silicon (Trainium, Graviton, etc.).
- Valuation/Risks MSFT (Buy): Our 12-month price target of $610 is based on a 28x P/E multiple to Microsoft's SNTM adjusted net income.
- Sizing the Consumer Agent Opportunity The report estimates consumer AI agents can lift global token consumption 12X by 2030. n Consumer AI queries are already a large and growing market, but the mix is shifting quickly as AI overviews and LLM agentic queries take share from traditional search.
- We prefer the following stocks: AMZN (Buy, $325 PT): We continue to see visibility into returns as AWS o revenues compound (growth reaccelerated to +28% year over year in Q1; new Goldman Sachs estimates for ~low 30s % year over year growth in FY26 & FY27) supported by a reported $364bn revenue backlog (not including an additional $100bn for a deal announced in Q2), driven by both AI workloads and building momentum around its custom silicon (Trainium, Graviton, etc.).
- ACN (Buy): Our 12-month price target of $300 is based on 20x our one-year forward earnings estimates.
- NVDA (Buy): Our 12-month price target of $250 is based on a 30X P/E multiple applied to our normalized EPS estimate of $8.25.
- At ~23 billion AI queries per day by 2030, up from ~5 billion in 2025, we estimate up to 30% will be directed to agents across search, shopping, travel, email, and other personal productivity functions.
- GOOGL (Buy, $450 PT): Alphabet is seeing momentum across its Cloud o business (+63% year over year in Q1 with backlog nearly doubling quarter over quarter to ~$460bn) and Search multi-modality, leveraging a full-stack approach as mgmt continues to see AI as repositioning the company for sustained growth.
- NET (Buy): Our 12-month price target of $250 is based on 27x Q5-Q8 revenue.
- AVGO (Buy): Our 12-month target price of $480 is based on 30X our normalized EPS estimate of $16.
- AMD (Buy): Our 12-month target price of $450 is based on a 30X P/E multiple applied to our normalized EPS estimate of $15.00.
- Moving past concepts to numbers: We see Agentic AI driving a dramatic increase in token consumption of 24X or 120 quadrillion tokens per month by 2030.
- We believe consumer agents will broaden usage away from episodic chats to utility beyond traditional search, driving 12X token consumption by 2030.
- Why now is the time - an economic inflection point for hyperscalers and model makers: Critically, we outline why we see an inflection in token economics ahead for hyperscalers and model providers, enabled by continued token cost declines (powered by leading semi companies driving 60%-70% lower annualized cost per token) and stabilizing token prices (which have moved from ~40% annual declines to flat or increasing pricing).

Risks, catalysts, and watch points
- In this report, we outline some of the likely use cases we see for Agentic AI across the enterprise and consumer sphere - and quantify potential upside to business outcomes, along with the investment levels required.
- In other words, the Agentic AI explosion in token consumption we model by 2030 may not only reflect a demand story, but also a margin expansion and profitability story across the AI value chain.
- ACN (Buy, $300 12-m PT, covered by Jim Schneider): The report expects Accenture o to see growing tailwinds from agentic adoption as enterprises increasingly move from AI pilots to scaled agent deployments, driving demand for integration, workflow redesign, governance, and change management.
- By 2030, our bottom-up framework (built on our simulated agents that validate real-world token intensity) suggests that global token demand could rise by 2,400% versus 2026 levels, with consumer agents potentially reaching ~60 quadrillion tokens per month and enterprise agents reaching ~56 quadrillion tokens per month (or 278 quadrillion by peak adoption in 2040), assuming adoption broadens.
- Simply put - the dramatic increase in token consumption we have modeled by 2030 may not only reflect a demand and revenue narrative, but also a margin expansion and profitability story across the AI value chain.
- In other words, we now believe the industry could be moving from a phase where inference economics were uncertain and potentially dilutive to margins to a phase where token growth increasingly drops through at attractive incremental margins.

Investment advice or portfolio implication
- Investment Implications For hyperscalers and model providers, we prefer the following stocks (covered n by Eric Sheridan): AMZN (Buy, $325 12-m PT): We continue to see visibility into returns as AWS o revenues compound, supported by a reported $364bn revenue backlog, driven by both AI workloads and rising momentum around its custom silicon (Trainium, Graviton, etc.).
- Valuation/Risks MSFT (Buy): Our 12-month price target of $610 is based on a 28x P/E multiple to Microsoft's SNTM adjusted net income.
- We prefer the following stocks: AMZN (Buy, $325 PT): We continue to see visibility into returns as AWS o revenues compound (growth reaccelerated to +28% year over year in Q1; new Goldman Sachs estimates for ~low 30s % year over year growth in FY26 & FY27) supported by a reported $364bn revenue backlog (not including an additional $100bn for a deal announced in Q2), driven by both AI workloads and building momentum around its custom silicon (Trainium, Graviton, etc.).

## OIL ANALYST Running Out of Oil A Large But Still Mostly Local Products Risk

PDF Summary - OIL ANALYST Running Out of Oil A Large But Still Mostly Local Products Risk

Source file:
- 1.OIL ANALYST Running Out of Oil A Large But Still Mostly Local Products Risk(1).pdf
Pages in representative file: 22
Readable text extracted from grouped file(s): 95,964 characters

Duplicate/logical-duplicate handling: this draft summarizes the following selected variants once:
- 1.OIL ANALYST Running Out of Oil A Large But Still Mostly Local Products Risk(1).pdf
- 5.OIL ANALYST_Running Out of Oil A Large But Still Mostly Local Products Risk.pdf

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, oil-market supply risk and inflation transmission, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- While total global stocks-the sum of visible n and invisible, crude and products, landed and on water, and commercial and strategic stocks-are unlikely to hit minimum operational levels this summer, the speed of depletion and supply losses in some regions and products are concerning, with easily accessible refined products buffers approaching very low levels fast.
- The most immediate shortages risks remain in petrochemical feedstocks (naphtha and LPG) and jet fuel and in EM Asia ex-China and Europe (jet fuel).
- Global oil stocks approaching their lowest level on an 8-year record is more n concerning from a depletion speed perspective than from an aggregate level perspective (for now).
- The report estimates total global oil stocks, including estimated "invisible" stocks o (mostly non-OECD refined products), at 101 days of global demand (DoD) now and at 98 days by end-May.
- While these aggregate stock estimates remain above the minimum 61 DoD of emergency stocks the EU requires and the minimum operational landed storage level for the global oil system estimated at ~30-40 DoD, they significantly understate the risks of country-product shortages given major differences across products and regions, and product export restrictions.

Key data and arguments
- The most immediate shortages risks remain in petrochemical feedstocks (naphtha and LPG) and jet fuel and in EM Asia ex-China and Europe (jet fuel).
- Naphtha stocks dropped 72% in UAE Fujairah and 37% in Northwest Europe ARA since end February, reflecting petrochemical tightness and limited alternatives for lost Gulf supply.
- Higher risks of refined products scarcity in Asia-Pacific and Europe (jet fuel). n While global oil stocks are not at critical levels (yet), a surplus in one o country-product market can't always resolve shortages elsewhere.
- Together with our European energy and transportation equity analysts, we o recently estimated that European commercial jet fuel inventories (excluding government emergency reserves) could fall below the IEA's critical 23-day shortage threshold in June.
- While only ~30% of products stocks are visible, they show rapid draws o outside export-restricting regions (e.g.
- While these aggregate stock estimates remain above the minimum 61 DoD of emergency stocks the EU requires and the minimum operational landed storage level for the global oil system estimated at ~30-40 DoD, they significantly understate the risks of country-product shortages given major differences across products and regions, and product export restrictions.
- Our estimates of supply of refined products and countries' own crude stocks point to higher risks of product scarcity in South Africa, India, Thailand, and Taiwan.
- The report estimates total global oil stocks, including estimated "invisible" stocks o (mostly non-OECD refined products), at 101 days of global demand (DoD) now and at 98 days by end-May.
- The report estimates very large declines in the supply of refined products (based on o crude and products trade volumes) in several Asian and African countries, especially for naphtha and LPG (petrochemicals), jet fuel, and fuel oil, but also for diesel.
- Assuming a similar 3 DoD monthly average pace of draws (consistent with a just over 10% deficit) over the next month would leave estimated global stocks at 98 DoD by end of May.
- That said, these global estimates mask significant local risks to supply, especially heading into the peak demand season in the Northern Hemisphere.
- The IEA requires its members to maintain oil stocks of at least 90 days of their net oil imports (crude and refined products) while EU countries must hold oil stocks of at least 61 days of consumption (if this level is higher than what the 90-days of net oil imports imply).
- Pipelines, refineries, and storage tanks must maintain minimum oil to operate.
- Our estimates suggest that the operational minimum storage level for the landed global oil system is between 30-40 days of demand.23 2 Our estimate of 30-40 days of demand as a minimum threshold for global storage is based on assumption that 1) a typical refinery will need 20 days of crude throughput; 2) 20% of crude storage in with floating roofs is required (assuming Jun 2020 levels were close to 100% of crude storage) 3) roughly 40mb/d of global pipeline capacity needs 30% of operational throughput for 2-3.

Risks, catalysts, and watch points
- While total global stocks-the sum of visible n and invisible, crude and products, landed and on water, and commercial and strategic stocks-are unlikely to hit minimum operational levels this summer, the speed of depletion and supply losses in some regions and products are concerning, with easily accessible refined products buffers approaching very low levels fast.
- The most immediate shortages risks remain in petrochemical feedstocks (naphtha and LPG) and jet fuel and in EM Asia ex-China and Europe (jet fuel).
- The report estimates total global oil stocks, including estimated "invisible" stocks o (mostly non-OECD refined products), at 101 days of global demand (DoD) now and at 98 days by end-May.
- While these aggregate stock estimates remain above the minimum 61 DoD of emergency stocks the EU requires and the minimum operational landed storage level for the global oil system estimated at ~30-40 DoD, they significantly understate the risks of country-product shortages given major differences across products and regions, and product export restrictions.
- Naphtha stocks dropped 72% in UAE Fujairah and 37% in Northwest Europe ARA since end February, reflecting petrochemical tightness and limited alternatives for lost Gulf supply.
- Higher risks of refined products scarcity in Asia-Pacific and Europe (jet fuel). n While global oil stocks are not at critical levels (yet), a surplus in one o country-product market can't always resolve shortages elsewhere.

Investment advice or portfolio implication
- The IEA requires its members to maintain oil stocks of at least 90 days of their net oil imports (crude and refined products) while EU countries must hold oil stocks of at least 61 days of consumption (if this level is higher than what the 90-days of net oil imports imply).
- Pipelines, refineries, and storage tanks must maintain minimum oil to operate.

- The Bank of Japan (BOJ) held its MPM on April 27-28, and, as we have been forecasting, decided to maintain its policy rate guidance on the overnight call rate (TONA) at 0.75% (by majority vote).
- Questioned on the decision to keep rates on hold amid high upside risks to inflation, Governor Ueda explained that the likelihood of the BOJ's forecast materializing is declining, and while attention should be paid to upside risks to inflation, the situation is not so urgent as to require an immediate rate hike.
- Questioned on this point, Governor Ueda said the wording was revised to avoid linking economic improvement with rate hikes, explaining that a rate hike is possible even with a growth slowdown in sight due to higher oil prices, if the economy is likely to avoid a severe adjustment and price development is in line with the BOJ's forecast, or if the risk of overshooting the trajectory rises.

- The report expects growth to accelerate, especially into CY27, and see the positive cycle continuing for the time being.

## Americas Business & Information Services Written Off but Still Winning Structural AI Risk...

PDF Summary - Americas Business & Information Services Written Off but Still Winning Structural AI Risk Across Information Services

Source file:
- 13. Americas Business & Information Services_ Written Off but Still Winning_ Structural AI Risk Across Information Services.pdf
Pages in representative file: 75
Readable text extracted from grouped file(s): 202,398 characters

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, rates, duration, and term-premium repricing, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk, gold positioning and real-rate/geopolitical hedges. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- We believe AI impacts vary materially by vertical, with adoption concentrated in repetitive and data intensive tasks that drive productivity gains inside existing workflows, while activities requiring deterministic precision, regulatory compliance, liability bearing judgment, or authoritative outputs remain difficult to replace.
- We introduce a segment level methodology to assess structural AI resilience across buckets including Proprietary Data, Regulatory Moat, Workflow Entrenchment, and Output Accountability, with AI Execution evaluated separately as a mitigating factor, and translate these structural assessments into company specific EPS sensitivities by modeling revenue growth and margin outcomes around our base case forecasts.
- Our assessment reveals wide dispersion across the universe, with high scorers such as VRSK, EFX, MCO, TRU, FICO, MSCI, and SPGI benefiting from overlapping structural protections, mid tier profiles at TRI, MH, and CSGP reflecting mixed exposure, and lower scoring models including FDS, CLVT, and IT more vulnerable to AI enabled substitution.
- Based on our AI risk assessments, we downgrade IT to Neutral from Buy, believe Buy-rated TRI is materially oversold relative to its Legal and Tax protections, and see selective upside in high scoring names where compressed valuations coincide with durable earnings power.
- AMERICAS BUSINESS & INFORMATION SERVICES George K.

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk, healthcare access, pricing, and demand expansion. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- With the Loss of Exclusivity (LoE) for semaglutide in key emerging markets (e.g., China, India, Brazil) in late March, the GLP-1 landscape is poised for disruption from generic drugs.
- This shift could have a significant impact on market dynamics and the GLP-1 supply chain.
- In this note, we analyze the potential disruption with - 1) a breakdown analysis of the manufacturing cost of generic semaglutide, and 2) update on the landscape and peptide capacity, highlighting the potential opportunities.
- Generic semaglutide could go down to US$10 per month: To better understand the potential pricing range for generic semaglutide, the key components of the manufacturing process have been broken down within and based on this analysis, we expect the pricing of generic semaglutide to be 1) c.US$50/month in the bull case (e.g., first-in-market, premium pen design), 2) c.US$10/month in a mature market (e.g., after volume-based procurement or VBP), and 3) c.US$2.5/month in the bear case assuming 25% GPM to cover SG&A.
- The first batch of Indian generic players are launching semaglutide at prices (US$14-US$44 per month) that are compatible with our analysis.

- Buying Options - Investors who buy call (put) options risk loss of the entire premium paid if the underlying security finishes below (above) the strike price at expiration.
- Investors who buy call or put spreads also risk a maximum loss of the premium paid.
- Investors who sell put or call spreads risk a maximum loss of the difference between the strikes less the premium received, while their maximum gain is the premium received.
- Cross-asset: Forecasts Exhibit 7: GOAL asset allocation recommendations and GS cross-asset forecasts Current 3m 12m Level 3m 6m 12 m 3m 6m 12 m Equities N OW S&P 500 ($) N N 7165 7200 7400 7600 0.8 3.9 7.2 Stoxx Europe 600 (â‚¬) N UW 611 605 615 625 -0.1 2.4 5.7 MSCI Asia-Pacific ex.
- Selling Options - Investors who sell calls on securities they do not own risk unlimited loss of the security price less the strike price.
- Investors who sell covered calls (sell calls while owning the underlying security) risk having to deliver the underlying security or pay the difference between the security price and the strike price, depending on whether the option is settled by physical delivery or cash-settled.
- Investors who sell puts risk loss of the strike price less the premium received for selling the put.

- Higher energy density, output and charging performance vs standard cylindrical positions tab-less as a margin accretive mix shift for the cylindrical segment overall.

- Hungary plant's utilization is targeted at c.70% in 2H26 with LFP line conversion, while targeting EV segment BEP in 2H26, subject to customer demand trajectory.
- ESS remains the key earnings driver; Data center-linked demand accelerating.
- According to SDI, US total ESS demand is expected to grow from 90 GWh in 2025 to 160 GWh in 2030 (c.12% CAGR).
- Tab-less cylindrical ramp is a near-term profitability catalyst.
- SDI guided tab-less share of cylindrical battery sales to exceed 20% in 2026 vs 3-4% in 2025, driven by BBU demand from AI data centers and professional power tool applications.
- Tab-less supply to BBU starts 2Q26 and to hybrid EVs from 2H26.

- So far, however, AI is boosting US inflation.
- We see three key ways in which AI is boosting consumer prices.
- First, strong n demand for AI infrastructure has raised the price of some key electronics inputs, which has increased computer accessories prices and will likely boost smartphone and computer prices in coming months.
- Second, the addition of new AI features to existing software has likely put some upward pressure on software prices over the last couple of years.

Core thesis
- LLC Macro Credit Views: Carrying on 27 April 2026 | 5:36PM EDT The report expects some modest spread widening through mid-year.
- Our directional view for spreads calls for some modest widening through mid-year, with a higher peak and a slower recovery for EUR spreads relative to their USD peers.
- In addition to a somewhat more challenging mix for growth, inflation, and monetary policy (relative to the start of the year) on account of the commodity market disruptions, we also expect an acceleration in corporate debt issuance as companies exit their 1Q2026 earnings blackout periods through late April and early May.
- For this reason, our forecast for 'wider' spreads still leaves most markets roughly in line with their three-year averages.
- Carry is likely to be the dominant driver of total returns in corporate credit, as we see limited scope for a total return 'boost' from material spread tightening.

Key data and arguments

- In the EUR market, valuations across the rating cohorts are somewhat more compressed, and the relatively weaker growth backdrop warrants more of an up-in-quality stance.
- We have a preference for As over BBBs and would not move too far up the quality spectrum, as we expect supply technicals in the EUR AA market will become a more pronounced headwind over time.
- For example, Alphabet and Amazon are already two of the top five issuers in the Bloomberg EUR AA Corporate Index, and we expect more hyperscaler issuance into this market as US-based firms diversify their financing sources.

- Our view on the Banks sector-which is the largest weight in the USD and EUR IG indices-is nuanced.
- In the USD market, we favor Money Centers over Regionals and Yankees and are more comfortable moving down the capital structure in Money Centers, although thin carry premium dampens broad enthusiasm for subordinated debt.
- In the EUR market, we have a more defensive capital structure allocation and prefer Senior over LT2.
- Relative value within IG: Favor BBBs over higher-rated cohorts in the USD market.

- Among non-adopters, AI incompatibility with the business and a lack of knowledge on AI capabilities were the most commonly cited barriers to adoption.

- In this report, we dive into i) AI GPU infrastructure rental (GPUaaS) market on its rationale, economics and risks, which has seen YTD pricing surges mirroring the US market, and attracted many new entrants due to the favorable returns; ii) power-rich Western China hubs as the new markets for capacity expansion, under the national strategy of "East Data, West Computing" and "Coordination between Computing Resources and Power".
- We initiate coverage on Range Intelligent (300442.SZ) at Buy with a discounted EV/EBITDA-based TP of Rmb117, and on Shanghai Athub (603881.SS) at Neutral with an EV/EBITDA-based TP of Rmb34.
- Compared to GDS/VNET which remain focused on data center operations, Range and Athub are transforming their portfolios by incorporating the GPUaaS business, though at a different pace, in addition to building new/retrofitting existing facilities to become AI-ready.
- Meanwhile, we evaluate capacity reserves of major operators in key hubs as one of the critical implications for mid-term capacity expansion potential, considering the strict control of new power quota approvals which promotes healthier supply-demand dynamics and potentially industry consolidation in the long term.

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, credit positioning and private-credit risk. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- 28 April 2026 | 10:08AM BST A common narrative among some market participants is that credit acts as a n so-called 'canary in the coal mine', with spreads flagging stress before it reaches equities or the real economy.
- In this Global Markets Daily, we test that proposition across past crisis episodes.
- Overall, we find limited historical evidence that credit has reliably led equities in drawdowns.
- More often, credit and equities have sold off together, including during the GFC n and the European debt crisis.
- Where credit did lead, the episodes were relatively few and include the 1998 Russia/LTCM crisis, the early 2000s dot-com unwind, and the 2014-16 oil shock.

Key data and arguments
- Credit has only led equities in a few risk-off episodes Looking across USD and EUR HY spreads vs. equities across eight major stress episodes since the late 1990s, there were a few episodes where credit spread widening preceded equities.
- More often, credit and equities have sold off together, including during the GFC n and the European debt crisis.
- From a positioning perspective, we continue to see risks skewed toward modestly wider spreads and prefer USD over EUR, given Europe's greater exposure to energy shocks.
- There are only a handful of cases âˆ’ including Russia/LTCM in 1998, the dot-com unwind, and the 2014-16 energy downturn âˆ’ in which spread widening clearly came ahead of an equity sell-off.
- perspective, we continue to see risks skewed toward modestly wider spreads and prefer USD over EUR, given Europe's greater exposure to energy shocks.
- Buy 3-month (May 21st) 11.45/12.00 EUR/NOK call spreads, opened February 20, 4.
- Credit spreads are not sending a warning signal and may be less likely to do so History suggests that whether credit leads a broader sell-off depends in large part on the nature of the shock.
- Relatedly, structural features of today's market may make index-level spreads a n less sensitive barometer of risk aversion.
- In 1998, for example, USD HY was still a relatively small market, at just $330 billion outstanding, and the Russia default ultimately fed into the LTCM crisis and broader equity weakness, making this one of the clearer examples where credit did act as an early warning signal.
- In Europe, the ECB's corporate sector purchase programme (CSPP), announced in March 2016 and implemented from June 2016, made the ECB a large and predictable buyer of EUR IG corporate bonds.
- From a positioning perspective, we continue to see credit risk-reward as skewed toward somewhat wider spreads and prefer USD over EUR, given Europe's greater sensitivity to energy-driven shocks.
- Where credit did lead, the episodes were relatively few and include the 1998 Russia/LTCM crisis, the early 2000s dot-com unwind, and the 2014-16 oil shock.
- Against that backdrop, global credit spreads remain tight and are not flashing clear warning signals.
- In this Global Markets Daily, we assess that proposition by examining the behavior of credit spreads and equities across past crisis episodes.

Risks, catalysts, and watch points
- Relatedly, structural features of today's market may make index-level spreads a n less sensitive barometer of risk aversion.
- From a positioning perspective, we continue to see risks skewed toward modestly wider spreads and prefer USD over EUR, given Europe's greater exposure to energy shocks.
- perspective, we continue to see risks skewed toward modestly wider spreads and prefer USD over EUR, given Europe's greater exposure to energy shocks.
- Credit has only led equities in a few risk-off episodes Looking across USD and EUR HY spreads vs. equities across eight major stress episodes since the late 1990s, there were a few episodes where credit spread widening preceded equities.
- If anything, the more common pattern is that spreads remain relatively rangebound ahead of a broader risk-off move while equities continue to rally.
- However, once equities start their decline as part of a risk-off move, we find that credit did not move ahead of time.

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, oil-market supply risk and inflation transmission, rates, duration, and term-premium repricing, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk. Core thesis
- In this Global Markets Daily, we construct various FX carry strategies and analyse their carry returns, spot performance, and sensitivity to different market variables.
- Carry levels across different FX carry strategies have remained stable over the n past year, and we think the sustained pricing out of rate cuts argues for a longer window of EM FX carry outperformance relative to local rates receivers.
- Across FX carry baskets, those with fewer currencies in the long/short legs have n outperformed over the past year and since the Iran conflict began.
- We think this reflects the positive correlation between carry levels and sensitivities to risk as well as diverging terms of trade dynamics at either end of the carry spectrum.
- In our view, this argues for a selective approach when constructing FX carry baskets, where carry levels, relative terms of trade shifts, and idiosyncratic developments all play important roles.

Key data and arguments
- Taking a long BRL, HUF, MXN and ZAR basket, our analysis suggests that USD n funding leads to one of the most risk-on expressions and one of the most negatively correlated with oil prices.
- For investors looking to neutralise these exposures, we think EUR, SEK and THB funding looks attractive: they lead to higher carry returns (and a more attractive carry-to-vol profile in the case of SEK) alongside added resilience to energy-price and risk-sentiment shifts.
- We also discuss our preferred carry longs (BRL, HUF, MXN and ZAR) and scan through funders that can improve the carry (or carry-to-vol) profile and add resilience to risk and oil price shocks (we prefer EUR, SEK, and THB).
- USD funding among the more risk-on expressions; EUR, SEK and THB funding leads to higher carry and greater resilience to energy price shifts Finally, we can look at a basket of our preferred longs - BRL, HUF, MXN and ZAR - against various funders in order to optimise for carry levels, carry-to-vol ratios, as well as the exposure to global market developments.

- We think this reflects the positive correlation between carry levels and sensitivities to risk as well as diverging terms of trade dynamics at either end of the carry spectrum.
- And, under our forecasts, the decline in real rates that we had previously expected for this year is now likely to be slower(Exhibit 4).
- On carry specifically, BRL and COP continue to have the highest carry by a wide margin and our economists' forecasts for real policy rates at year-end are now higher than they were ahead of the Iran conflict (that is, 2026Q4 policy rate forecasts have been revised higher by more than 2027Q4 inflation forecasts have) (Exhibit 4).
- Not only has the Rand underperformed its high-carry, high-beta peers, but it is also supported by a constructive local picture on both the fiscal and monetary policy sides (we now forecast 50bp of SARB hikes this year).
- FX carry baskets with fewer currencies have outperformed over the past year, with marginal outperformance of long/short versus long-only strategies We start by constructing various FX carry baskets with long/short, long-only and short-only strategies across EM and G10 currencies (both jointly and separately) and with 2-5 currencies in each leg.
- However, between the two, long/short baskets mechanically yield higher carry returns (Exhibit 2), leading to greater outperformance in total return terms relative to the long-only baskets.
- HUF is one of the preferred medium-term longs supported by the significant shift in economic policy after the elections as it relates to both EU funds (and the broader relation with the EU) and the potential for Euro adoption.
- Carry levels and carry-to-vol ratios screen as more attractive versus the Euro, and we have an open short EUR/HUF trade recommendation.
- We remain bearish on the Asia high-yielders (IDR, PHP, INR) given their limited exposure to global risk sentiment (which has been supporting other high-beta energy importers like ZAR) and the negative external balance impact of higher-for-longer energy prices.

- Second, the overlay of terms of trade dynamics with both carry and risk: the higher carry currencies in EM (BRL, COP) and G10 (NOK, AUD) are energy exporters that have benefited from the higher energy price environment (Exhibit 5 ).

Core thesis
- This is unsurprising given the recent vol in energy and equity markets, but we think other factors are at play as well.
- First, while rates markets have seen exceptionally large moves throughout the n shock, the moves across G10 markets have generally been directionally uniform in response to the ebb and flow in energy prices.
- This has driven lower realised vol in rate differentials than in outright rates, and it is the former that matters more for FX markets.
- Second, FX's relationship to nominal rate differentials specifically has broken n down in recent months, while the relationship to real rates has remained more stable.
- We find that this is typically the case in supply-driven inflation regimes, and we think the ongoing energy shock is a clear example of this.

Key data and arguments
- Leveraging the San Francisco Fed's decomposition of headline PCE inflation into supply and demand drivers, we find that demand-led inflation regimes typically produce a positive relationship between EUR/USD and EU-US inflation differentials (with a full-sample beta of +0.54), while this relationship is closer to neutral under supply-led inflation regimes (with a beta of +0.17) (Exhibit 5).

- EUR/USD's relationship to nominal rate differentials has broken down in recent weeks, with a rolling 3-month beta having fallen sharply to below zero.
- Real rate differentials meanwhile help to strip out these effects, and have produced a more stable beta for EUR/USD recently (Exhibit 3).

- EUR/USD's declining beta to inflation differentials (and hence to nominal rate differentials) in the currency energy-driven supply shock is consistent with that broader finding.
- Consistent with the evolving beta of daily returns, we find that EUR/USD's beta to nominal rates dropped sharply after the onset of the energy shock at the end of February.
- Narrowing in on 5-minute periods where rate differentials are shifting but oil is relatively stable, we find that EUR/USD's beta to nominal rates has fallen by less, and has been positive so far in April (Exhibit 6).
- This is unsurprising given the scale of the spillovers to FX from energy prices and risk appetite in the wake of the conflict in the Middle East, but in our view, there are other factors driving this result as well.

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, oil-market supply risk and inflation transmission, rates, duration, and term-premium repricing, credit positioning and private-credit risk, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- Energy prices remain the focal point for rates markets, but smaller responses to energy upside have left rates volatility lower than in March.
- US rates are still lacking the potential catalysts to durably lower yields that would come from either de-escalatory relief or growth downside concerns.
- But the higher starting level of yields and rates' diminished sensitivity to oil moves continue to favor positive carry expressions for now, with inflation longs still a useful hedge against more protracted and/or disruptive outcomes.
- The gradual rise in energy prices and inflation risk were a headwind to carry trades in Europe ahead of the ECB and BoE meetings.
- We favor long sovereign credit and long inflation in Europe, while we prefer front-end longs in Gilts after a period of 10y outperformance on the curve.

Key data and arguments
- The gradual rise in energy prices and inflation risk were a headwind to carry trades in Europe ahead of the ECB and BoE meetings.
- We favor long sovereign credit and long inflation in Europe, while we prefer front-end longs in Gilts after a period of 10y outperformance on the curve.
- Our valuation framework based on energy prices, core inflation, the euro currency and the level of nominal yields points to upside risk for intermediate forwards, such as 2y2y (Exhibit 5).
- The shift in on the curve of JGB underperformance likely reflects an improved long-end supply/demand balance as well as the natural progression of risks that we would expect to extend if longer-term inflation concerns persist and the BOJ maintains its gradual approach.
- That keeps the near-term bias towards finding ways to earn carry and insulating against the risk of higher inflation (more below) even as our medium-term views remain for lower yields.
- As we have observed further out the curve, regressing the changes in sequential inflation implied by the monthly fixings on the corresponding oil future contract suggests that this can at least be partially tied to the lack in risk premium in the oil curve, with a combination of rapid declines in oil demand and anticipation of Hormuz reopening helping to constrain longer-dated futures prices despite still-low flows.
- While a range of factors differentiate the risks today from 2022, we nonetheless continue to see value in breakeven longs as a hedge to scenarios where oil prices are higher for longer or markets price greater risk of a broadening inflationary impact from supply chain disruptions.
- The pace of accumulation is not all that different from last year-the Flow of Funds data shows commercial banks purchased about $200bn USTs in 2025-but the changes to the eSLR should, in theory, reduce the constraint on G-SIBs' ability to add riskless assets in particular.
- Support measures announced so far in France have been small and targeted - close to â‚¬1bn - and importantly, the government has also announced 6bn worth of spending cuts in order to maintain its deficit objectives for 2026, suggesting an improvement in France's historically looser fiscal reaction function.
- We revise the target and stop on our beta-weighted 10y inflation long recommendation to 1.65% and 1.53%, respectively.
- Commercial n banks' steady buying of US Treasuries appears to have continued over the first several months of 2026, with H.8 data showing a $70bn increase in Treasury and agency holdings over the first fourteen weeks of the year.
- While we think the CAD curve has value on a standalone basis and view the 2s5s segment as better insulated against oil volatility than 2s10s without a significant carry differential, cross-market steepeners vs USD or AUD (where higher inflation concerns are pointing to the usual rates reaction to ToT shocks) are reasonable expressions to insulate against global flattening pressure (Exhibit 4).
- Our economists expect the ECB to hold next week but to signal willingness to tighten should signs of inflation persistence emerge-they maintain their expectation for a couple of hikes in June and September.
- US rates are still lacking the potential catalysts to durably lower yields that would come from either de-escalatory relief or growth downside concerns.

- With the Fed likely to retain its "wait and see" approach given inflation uncertainty and stability in the labor market data, the distance from a clear offramp leaves rate risks two-sided in the near term.
- That keeps the near-term bias towards finding ways to earn carry and insulating against the risk of higher inflation (more below) even as our medium-term views remain for lower yields.

Core thesis
- EM Equities: Forging Ahead after the Rebound.
- Notwithstanding the recent n volatility in crude oil prices, the resilience of EM equity performance following the US-Iran ceasefire has persisted.
- MSCI EM is now ~2% above pre-conflict levels and +18% from conflict period lows, outperforming DM ex-US peers, which still trade ~4% below pre-conflict levels.
- AI/Tech-heavy Korea and Taiwan have continued to lead the gains, while oil exporters have outperformed oil importers.
- Micro fundamentals have been supportive too, as 1QCY26 earnings for MSCI EM are tracking ahead of expectations at 38%yoy vs 28% at the start of the season, again with an outsized contribution from North Asia.

- LLC US Daily: Forecasting Productivity Growth: Slow to Adjust, Quick to Overshoot 5 May 2026 | 8:05AM EDT Last cycle's productivity pessimism has given way to a somewhat brighter n outlook as productivity growth has accelerated from its pre-pandemic pace and excitement about a coming tailwind from AI has grown.
- Admittedly, economists have a humbling track record in forecasting productivity growth.
- In today's Daily, we look at the history of US productivity growth forecasts to draw lessons for the current outlook.
- Using data from the Survey of Professional Forecasters (SPF) since the early n 1990s, we draw two main conclusions.
- First, professional forecasters have performed no better than a naÃ¯ve forecast based on long-run historical averages of US productivity growth.

Key data and arguments
- While we expect US nonfarm business labor productivity growth to average n around 2.3% over 2026-2030, most alternative forecasts currently cluster at or slightly below the 10-year trailing average of roughly 2%-consistent with the historical pattern we document.
- As Exhibit 1 shows, forecast errors from the SPF are nearly identical to those generated by simply using a real-time 30-year trailing average to forecast 10-year-ahead nonfarm business productivity growth1-with both approaches yielding average absolute forecast errors of around 0.7pp.2 Forecasts based on shorter trailing averages-or combinations of recent and long-run averages-perform worse.
- The report expects nonfarm business productivity growth to average around 2.3% through 2030-with an AI-driven acceleration toward the end of the decade-while most alternative medium-run forecasts cluster at or slightly below 2% (Exhibit 4).4 These lower forecasts are consistent with the historical pattern we document: forecasters are gradually adjusting their estimates to reflect the recent acceleration in productivity growth but remain anchored near the 10-year trailing average of slightly below 2%.
- The 2.1% baseline forecast sits close to the slow-adoption scenario forecast (2.0%) and well below the moderate- and rapid-adoption scenario forecasts (2.5% and 3.5%, respectively), suggesting that most forecasters are quite optimistic about AI's potential but are currently assuming a relatively slow rate of AI adoption through 2030 (Exhibit 5, left panel).
- Other recent estimates also suggest that economists see a wide range of possible medium-run productivity gains from AI-from a modest 0.1pp annual boost over the next decade estimated by the Congressional Budget Office to 0.4-1.3pp estimated by OECD economists depending on the pace of adoption (Exhibit 5, right panel).6 5 Karger et al.

- The gap partly reflects our more positive view on AI's likely contribution to future productivity growth: responses to a recent survey suggest that most forecasters are quite optimistic about AI's potential but are assuming only a slow pace of AI adoption through 2030.

Core thesis
- Asia still absorbing most of the LNG supply shock.
- China demand still the biggest miss vs our expectations...
- We've also observed weaker LNG demand in Japan and South Korea vs our expectations, likely driven by a combination of comfortable inventory levels and petrochemical demand destruction owing to naphtha shortages, which in turn have reduced chemical companies' operating rates and, with it, their natural gas demand. ...Which we think will partially extend into the rest of the year.
- In addition to n offering a meaningful offset to global LNG supply losses this month, leaving European LNG imports only modestly down from March, this weakness in Asia LNG demand suggests a similar trend for the remainder of summer.
- To be clear, while we expect Asia LNG demand to recover sequentially from its April lows, partly as some chemical companies make alternative arrangements to source naphtha and other chemical feedstocks, the gas demand recovery will likely be gradual.

Key data and arguments
- As a result, we n maintain our view that, as long as European natural gas prices continue to maximize gas-to-coal switching this summer, at least 5 EUR/MWh above coal generation costs currently at 35 EUR/MWh,1 NW Europe should be on track to take its gas inventories to just over 80% full by end-October (Exhibit 6 and Exhibit 7).
- We also maintain our 40 EUR/MWh 4Q26 TTF forecast (and $14.65/mmBtu for JKM), under forwards at 45 EUR ($16.15/mmBtu for JKM) (Exhibit 8).
- We already assume 2029 China/India LNG imports up by 75%/61% vs 2025 levels, so the risk that Asia LNG demand disappoints leaves risks to our 2028/29 TTF and JKM price forecasts skewed to the downside, in turn posing a risk that, at some point from 2028, US LNG exports might have to be temporarily curtailed to solve the global LNG market oversupply.

- High-frequency data for n April suggest Asia LNG demand has weakened further vs March, with the region absorbing an even larger share (over 70% currently vs mid-60s last month) of the ongoing LNG supply shock driven by the interrupted flows through the Strait of Hormuz (SoH) (Exhibit 1).
- In addition to n offering a meaningful offset to global LNG supply losses this month, leaving European LNG imports only modestly down from March, this weakness in Asia LNG demand suggests a similar trend for the remainder of summer.

Core thesis
- Stable growth: Chinese Q1 real GDP growth was reported at 5.0% yoy, the same n pace as that for 2025 and better than the market expected.
- Despite steady headline growth, sectoral disparities widened.
- Export value jumped 14.7% yoy in Q1, while property and auto sales experienced double-digit declines.
- With the Strait of Hormuz still closed and energy prices elevated, we expect sequential real GDP growth to slow from 5.3% qoq annualized in Q1 to 4.0% in Q2.
- Stable markets: Chinese financial markets have demonstrated notable resilience n amid external shocks.

- Domestic fuel prices have risen about 20% since the Iran war began.
- Chinese exports to the Middle East plunged 45% yoy in March, reducing China's total exports by nearly 3pp (Exhibit 3).

Risks, catalysts, and watch points
- Stable policy: With growth on track but uncertainty high, we expect the PBOC to n maintain ample liquidity in Q2 for risk management.
- The "strong exports and weak domestic demand" pattern that we identified two years ago not only persisted but became more extreme into early 2026.
- In the near term, continued trade disruptions in the Middle East, lower demand from low-income oil-importing trading partners, and reduced real household income will likely weigh on activity in the coming months.
- First, China's dominance in new-energy products should support exports following the global energy supply shock.
- Second, resilient supply chains in China may allow producers to gain market share in sectors facing ex-China supply disruptions.
- First, the Chinese government not only built up oil reserves before the Middle East conflict, but also prioritized security in recent years-from food supply to trade diversification-which has strengthened the economy's ability to withstand external shocks such as a potential closure of the Strait of Hormuz.

Core thesis
- LLC Eye on Freight: Amazon Weighs On Transport Shares - But Fundamentals Today Should be in Focus 4 May 2026 | 7:05PM EDT Bottom line: Transport shares sold off sharply today (transports -5%, parcel -10%, RXO -10%, CHRW -9%) on the back of a news release from Amazon that it is launching Amazon Supply Chain Services (ASCS) with the intent to open its various freight and logistics services to all different businesses, not just Amazon sellers (link); i.e. offer third party competition and not just to those customers.
- That said, our interpretation is that the various services offered - including truckload, brokerage, LTL, parcel, etc are all services/capabilities previously offered and that ASCS is a broad-based umbrella or hub with which a shipper can go to utilize the various services already in existence.
- While we are not saying that this is not a competitive threat, we are saying that Amazon is one competitor of many across the transport landscape, and it remains to be seen if it currently has the scope to truly replace incumbents with networks dedicated to moving freight in its various forms.
- The truth is the US freight industry is significant in size - and should we fully emerge from the freight recession there should be ample growth opportunity across the transport landscape.
- For instance, the truckload market is very fragmented and is typically not influenced by one competitor, while the LTL sector has not had a new competitor in many years owing to the extensive breakbulk network required to be a national LTL carrier (note that Amazon's map - see below - indicates that at this point it is not fully national coverage).

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, property-sector stabilization and policy support, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- Amid concern over the impact of heightened airfares arising from the Middle East conflict and potential traffic diversion from the Spring breaks and Qingming festival in late March/early April, we believe market expectation was not particularly high heading into the Labor Day holidays (May 1-5th), with the Ministry of Transportation forecasting merely +4% yoy growth in cross-regional personnel mobility (vs. +8% during the CNY holidays).
- Indeed, the various data points we gathered from government sources and across industries (i.e., airlines, hotels, duty-free, tourist destinations, Macau, HK) suggest such a magnitude of slowdown to +4% yoy with fewer people taking air flight (-5%) in view of the higher airfares (+12% yoy).
- Some instead traveled by railways (+5%), buses (+7%) and/or drive on their own (+4%).
- We also saw similar trend in outbound travels as the National Immigration Administration disclosed that cross-border traffic only grew +4% yoy to ~2.4mn dragged by -4% yoy decline in air traffic against +9% airfare increase.
- Given more expensive airfare to distant destinations, Chinese residents tended to travel short-haul as reflected by outpaced flight capacity growth to Malaysia (+26%), Philippines (+35% helped by visa-free policies effective in Jan), Korea (+13%), Thailand (+12%), making up for the shortfall to Japan (-53%) where bilateral diplomatic tension with China is still ongoing.

- Hong Kong property names we cover with retail exposure have performed well, SHKP (+5%), Henderson (+5%), Wharf REIC (+2%) though perhaps more supported by stronger-than-expected housing price recovery +8% ytd tracking ahead of our above-consensus +12% forecast for the full year (see our sector report on Feb 18, Henderson Land, Buy (on CL) on May 4).
- Share prices of our covered leisure/travel names were broadly stable, except for Neutral-rated CTGDF (-4%) and selective hotel names such as Sell-rated Jinjiang (-5%) and Neutral-rated BTG (-4%).

## Global FX Trader Supply in the Balance

PDF Summary - Global FX Trader Supply in the Balance

Source file:
- 9.Global FX Trader_ Supply in the Balance (1).pdf
Pages in representative file: 14
Readable text extracted from grouped file(s): 51,062 characters

Conclusion
The document's central read is about AI adoption and infrastructure demand, rates, duration, and term-premium repricing, EV execution, margins, and product-cycle risk. The opening material and highest-signal data points indicate that the author is trying to identify what changed, which variables matter most for valuation or macro pricing, and where investors should focus for the next catalyst. In practical portfolio terms, the summary below separates the thesis, the supporting data, and the investable implications.

Core thesis
- Our thoughts on USD, BRL, GBP, CAD, ILS, INR, AUD & NZD, South East Asia FX, EGP and the FX-Rates Relationship USD: The curious case of the shrinking supply shock.
- We have maintained that n the ramifications of the conflict in the Middle East will affect economic data, and FX returns, even after peak uncertainty.
- Higher energy prices and product shortages are rearranging global current account balances and dampening growth momentum, and relative FX returns are increasingly reflecting this differentiation.
- We have revised our global growth forecasts lower, with smaller revisions in the US and other energy-insulated economies.
- Our economists are now well below consensus in APAC ex-China, and marginally below consensus in the Euro area, with a widening gap to the US, and our 3-month FX forecasts reflect this with broad Dollar depreciation delayed.

Key data and arguments
- However, with still-sparse traffic through the Strait and nascent signs of more widespread supply pressures-most prominently in the Euro area PMIs-markets should be more wary of continued upside risks to commodity prices, and mindful that higher-for-longer energy prices have an almost-mechanical impact on current account balances that matter for FX.
- In that respect, we still believe that European currencies in particular underprice the risk of a more noticeable energy constraint, even as the market has moved slightly in this direction over the last week.
- Moreover, to the extent that higher inflationary pressures keep the BCB on a more cautious easing path (our economists now expect a 25bp cut at next week's meeting), the carry component of total returns will remain even more supported, and FX longs will screen as more attractive than rates receivers.
- In our view, expressing BRL longs in a more risk-neutral format, for instance with CLP funding, would be an effective way of adding resilience.
- Our thoughts on USD, BRL, GBP, CAD, ILS, INR, AUD & NZD, South East Asia FX, EGP and the FX-Rates Relationship USD: The curious case of the shrinking supply shock.
- Our economists are now well below consensus in APAC ex-China, and marginally below consensus in the Euro area, with a widening gap to the US, and our 3-month FX forecasts reflect this with broad Dollar depreciation delayed.
- To reflect recent market moves and the balance of risks going forward, we revise our USD/BRL forecasts lower to 4.90, 5.00, 5.00 in 3-, 6- and 12-months (from 5.20, 5.30, 5.30 previously).
- We think this BRL relative outperformance has further to go as long as energy prices remain elevated but do not lead to weaker risk sentiment.
- BI also announced that it would allow primary dealers (subject to approvals) to sell USDIDR NDFs, as part of its efforts to deepen financial markets.
- With this in mind, we think that the main near-term risk to BRL returns is a reversal of the recent risk recovery.
- Still, we expect focus on the election to only pick-up in a few months, whereas in the near-term we expect the terms of trade and risk implications of the conflict to continue to dominate the price action.
- This is not only due to this tight correlation to tech stocks, but also because geopolitical risks for USD/ILS remain two-sided-with scope for higher Israel-specific premium to be priced on one hand, but also the potential for a lower threat from regional adversaries on the other-and thus are unlikely to provide a clear directional view while uncertainty remains elevated.
- However, over time, we think the currency's increasing overvaluation signal (now at over 14% vs the USD on our GSDEER model) will act as a restraint to further appreciation.
- Taken together, we think these carry, reserve and valuation buffers should (i) contain spot depreciation against negative geopolitical headlines given a still weak currency relative to pre-war levels, and should (ii) buffer total returns from such sell-offs should they occur.

Risks, catalysts, and watch points
- Our thoughts on USD, BRL, GBP, CAD, ILS, INR, AUD & NZD, South East Asia FX, EGP and the FX-Rates Relationship USD: The curious case of the shrinking supply shock.
- We have maintained that n the ramifications of the conflict in the Middle East will affect economic data, and FX returns, even after peak uncertainty.
- It is possible that global supply is proving to be more elastic than our GDP forecasts imply, which would leave us too cautious on cyclical currencies like AUD and too optimistic on the Dollar, especially in NJA.
- However, with still-sparse traffic through the Strait and nascent signs of more widespread supply pressures-most prominently in the Euro area PMIs-markets should be more wary of continued upside risks to commodity prices, and mindful that higher-for-longer energy prices have an almost-mechanical impact on current account balances that matter for FX.
- In that respect, we still believe that European currencies in particular underprice the risk of a more noticeable energy constraint, even as the market has moved slightly in this direction over the last week.

- Over the short-term (and into the company's Investor Day in 2H May), we would expect investor focus to remain on these two debates as well as the broader ongoing debate about the potential impact that AI might have on the audio landscape in the years ahead.

When no rating appears, the relevant advice is thematic: use the data to size exposure, identify second-order beneficiaries, and define stop-loss/watch-list variables around the risks listed above.

- æ·±å…¥ç ”ç©¶è¿™ä¸ªä¸»é¢˜ï¼Œå®Œæˆ äº†å‰ ä¸‰ç« å Žå°±æƒ´æƒ´ä¸ å®‰åœ°æŠŠç¨¿å­ ç»™æ´›å¨ æ•™æŽˆ è¿‡ç›®ï¼Œä»–è¯»å Žè¯´ï¼š"ä½ ä¸€å®šè¦ å†™ä¸‹åŽ»ã€‚"è¿™å°±æ˜¯å¤§å®¶é£ŽèŒƒï¼ˆæ´›å¨ æ•™æŽˆ102 å² é€ ä¸–ï¼Œä»–ä¸€ç›´æ˜¯æˆ‘æœ€çƒ­å¿ƒã€ æœ€ä¸¥åŽ‰çš„æ‰¹è¯„è€…ï¼‰ã€‚åœ¨ä»–çš„å¸®åŠ©ä¸‹ï¼Œæˆ‘ ç¡®å®šäº†è¦ å†™çš„å†…å®¹ã€‚ æ—¢ç„¶å†³å®šäº†ä¹¦çš„å†…å®¹ï¼Œå°±å¾—èµ·ä¸ªä¹¦å  ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸º" ç» æµŽå­¦" ï¼ˆeconomicsï¼‰è¿™ä¸ªè¯ å¯¹æ  å ‡é”€é‡ æ²¡ä»€ä¹ˆå¥½å¤„ï¼Œä¾¿ç»žå°½è„‘æ± åœ°æƒ³æ‰¾ä¸ª æ›¿ä»£è¯ ã€‚æˆ‘çš„ç¬¬äºŒé¡¿é‡ è¦ çš„å ˆé¤ æ˜¯ä¸Žå¼—é›·å¾·é‡Œå…‹Â·åˆ˜æ˜“æ–¯Â·è‰¾ä¼¦ ï¼ˆFrederick Lewis Allenï¼‰å…±åº¦çš„ã€‚ä»–æ˜¯ã€Šå“ˆç €ã€‹ï¼ˆHarper'sï¼‰æ ‚å¿—çš„ ç¼–è¾‘ï¼Œå¯¹æˆ‘é žå¸¸å ‹å¥½ï¼Œä¹Ÿç»™è¿‡æˆ‘å¾ˆå¤šå¸®åŠ©ï¼Œæˆ‘ä¹Ÿä¸ºä»–å†™è¿‡ä¸€äº›æ–‡ç« ã€‚ å…¶é—´æˆ‘å ‘ä»–è¯‰è¯´äº†å –ä¹¦å  çš„è‹¦æ ¼ã€‚å°½ç®¡æˆ‘çŸ¥é “"é‡‘é’±"ä¸€è¯ ä¸ å¤ªå ˆé€‚ï¼Œ ä½†æˆ‘è¿˜æ˜¯å¯¹ä»–è¯´ï¼Œæˆ‘æ‰“ç®—æŠŠä¹¦å  å®šä¸ºã€Šé‡‘é’±å“²å­¦å®¶ã€‹ï¼ˆThe Money Philosophersï¼‰ã€‚ä»–å¯¹æˆ‘è¯´ï¼š"ä½ çš„æ„ æ€ æ˜¯'ä¸–ä¿—çš„'ï¼ˆworldlyï¼‰ã€‚"æˆ‘ è¯´ï¼š"è¿™é¡¿é¥­æˆ‘è¯·ã€‚" æˆ‘å¯¹ã€Šä¸–ä¿—å“²å­¦å®¶ã€‹è¿™ä¸ªä¹¦å  å¾ˆæ»¡æ„ ï¼Œä½†å‡ºç‰ˆå•†ä¸ è¿™ä¹ˆæƒ³ã€‚è¿™æœ¬ ä¹¦ä¸Šå¸‚å Žä»¤æ‰€æœ‰äººæƒŠè®¶çš„æ˜¯ï¼Œå‡ºç‰ˆå•†å»ºè®®æŠŠä¹¦å  æ”¹ä¸ºã€Šä¼Ÿå¤§çš„ç» æµŽå­¦ å®¶ã€‹ï¼ˆThe Great Economistsï¼‰ã€‚å¹¸å¥½æ²¡è¿™ä¹ˆå šã€‚å ¯èƒ½ä»–ä»¬ä»¥ä¸ºï¼Œäºº.

Key data and arguments
- ç¬¬7ç‰ˆåº è¨€ æˆ‘å¤§çº¦åœ¨46å¹´å‰ å†™äº†è¿™æœ¬ä¹¦ï¼Œè¿™æ˜¯ç¬¬ä¸ƒæ¬¡ä¿®è®¢ï¼ŒçŽ°åœ¨ã€Šç» æµŽå­¦å®¶ åˆ°åº•åœ¨æƒ³ä»€ä¹ˆï¼šä»Žäºšå½“Â·æ–¯å¯†åˆ°å‡¯æ ©æ–¯ã€‹çš„"å¹´é¾„"æ¯”æˆ‘å½“å¹´å†™ä¹¦æ—¶çš„å¹´ é¾„å¤§å¤šäº†ã€‚è¿™æœ¬ä¹¦çš„ç”Ÿå‘½å‘¨æœŸå¦‚æ­¤ä¹‹é•¿æ˜¯æˆ‘å§‹æ–™æœªå Šçš„ã€‚å†™è¿™æœ¬ä¹¦ æ—¶ï¼Œæˆ‘è¿˜åœ¨è¯»ç ”ç©¶ç”Ÿã€‚åœ¨è°ˆå Šç¬¬ä¸ƒç‰ˆï¼Œä¹Ÿæ˜¯æœ€å Žä¸€æ¬¡çš„é‡ è¦ æ”¹åŠ¨ä¹‹ å‰ ï¼Œæˆ‘è¦ å…ˆè°ˆè°ˆå½“å¹´çš„å†™ä½œç» è¿‡ã€‚ 20ä¸–çºª50å¹´ä»£åˆ æˆ‘åœ¨è¯»ç ”ç©¶ç”Ÿï¼Œé‚£æ—¶æˆ‘ä»¥è‡ªç”±æ’°ç¨¿è°‹ç”Ÿï¼Œå‡ºäºŽéœ€ è¦ æˆ–å ¶ç„¶çš„ç›®çš„ï¼Œæœ‰æ—¶æˆ‘å†™çš„æ–‡ç« ä¸Žç» æµŽå­¦æ¯«ä¸ æ²¾è¾¹ã€‚ç”±äºŽè¿™äº›æ–‡ ç« ï¼Œè¥¿è’™&èˆ’æ–¯ç‰¹å‡ºç‰ˆç¤¾ï¼ˆSimon & Schusterï¼‰çš„é«˜çº§ç¼–è¾‘çº¦ç‘Ÿå¤«Â·å·´ æ ©æ–¯ï¼ˆJoseph Barnesï¼‰é‚€æˆ‘å…±è¿›å ˆé¤ ï¼ŒæŽ¢è®¨å „ç§ å‡ºä¹¦çš„æ„ å ‘ï¼Œä½†æˆ‘ä»¬ æ²¡æœ‰æ‰¾åˆ°ä¸€ä¸ªå ˆé€‚çš„ä¸»é¢˜ã€‚å½“æ²™æ‹‰ä¸Šæ¡Œæ—¶æˆ‘æœ‰ç‚¹å¤±æœ›ï¼Œæˆ‘æƒ³æˆ‘çš„ç¬¬ä¸€ æ¬¡å‡ºç‰ˆå•†çš„å ˆé¤ å¾ˆéš¾ä»¥è¾¾æˆ ç­¾çº¦æ”¶å°¾äº†ã€‚ä¸ è¿‡ï¼Œå·´æ ©æ–¯å€’æ²¡é‚£ä¹ˆå®¹æ˜“ æ°”é¦ ã€‚ä»–å¼€å§‹è¯¢é—®æˆ‘åœ¨æ–°å­¦é™¢å¤§å­¦çš„ç ”ç©¶ç”Ÿå­¦ä¹ æƒ…å†µï¼Œæˆ‘å…´è‡´å‹ƒå‹ƒ åœ°è Šèµ·äº†ä¸€é—¨æœ‰å…³äºšå½“Â·æ–¯å¯†ï¼ˆAdam Smithï¼‰çš„ç ”è®¨è¯¾ã€‚è¿™é—¨è¯¾ç‰¹åˆ« æœ‰è¶£ï¼Œç”±é˜¿é “å¤«Â·æ´›å¨ ï¼ˆAdolph Loweï¼‰æ•™æŽˆä¸»è®²ã€‚åœ¨ç”œç‚¹è¿˜æ²¡ä¸Šæ¡Œ æ—¶ï¼Œæˆ‘ä»¬éƒ½æ„ è¯†åˆ°ï¼Œæˆ‘æ‰¾åˆ°äº†é€‚å ˆçš„å†™ä½œä¸»é¢˜ã€‚ç­‰åˆ°ä¸‹ä¸€æ¬¡è¯¾ç»“æ Ÿ æ—¶ï¼Œæˆ‘å…´å†²å†²åœ°å‘Šè¯‰æ´›å¨ æ•™æŽˆï¼Œæˆ‘æ‰“ç®—å†™ä¸€éƒ¨æœ‰å…³ç» æµŽæ€ æƒ³å ²æ¼”è¿›çš„ è‘—ä½œã€‚.

- æ·±å…¥ç ”ç©¶è¿™ä¸ªä¸»é¢˜ï¼Œå®Œæˆ äº†å‰ ä¸‰ç« å Žå°±æƒ´æƒ´ä¸ å®‰åœ°æŠŠç¨¿å­ ç»™æ´›å¨ æ•™æŽˆ è¿‡ç›®ï¼Œä»–è¯»å Žè¯´ï¼š"ä½ ä¸€å®šè¦ å†™ä¸‹åŽ»ã€‚"è¿™å°±æ˜¯å¤§å®¶é£ŽèŒƒï¼ˆæ´›å¨ æ•™æŽˆ102 å² é€ ä¸–ï¼Œä»–ä¸€ç›´æ˜¯æˆ‘æœ€çƒ­å¿ƒã€ æœ€ä¸¥åŽ‰çš„æ‰¹è¯„è€…ï¼‰ã€‚åœ¨ä»–çš„å¸®åŠ©ä¸‹ï¼Œæˆ‘ ç¡®å®šäº†è¦ å†™çš„å†…å®¹ã€‚ æ—¢ç„¶å†³å®šäº†ä¹¦çš„å†…å®¹ï¼Œå°±å¾—èµ·ä¸ªä¹¦å  ã€‚æˆ‘è®¤ä¸º" ç» æµŽå­¦" ï¼ˆeconomicsï¼‰è¿™ä¸ªè¯ å¯¹æ  å ‡é”€é‡ æ²¡ä»€ä¹ˆå¥½å¤„ï¼Œä¾¿ç»žå°½è„‘æ± åœ°æƒ³æ‰¾ä¸ª æ›¿ä»£è¯ ã€‚æˆ‘çš„ç¬¬äºŒé¡¿é‡ è¦ çš„å ˆé¤ æ˜¯ä¸Žå¼—é›·å¾·é‡Œå…‹Â·åˆ˜æ˜“æ–¯Â·è‰¾ä¼¦ ï¼ˆFrederick Lewis Allenï¼‰å…±åº¦çš„ã€‚ä»–æ˜¯ã€Šå“ˆç €ã€‹ï¼ˆHarper'sï¼‰æ ‚å¿—çš„ ç¼–è¾‘ï¼Œå¯¹æˆ‘é žå¸¸å ‹å¥½ï¼Œä¹Ÿç»™è¿‡æˆ‘å¾ˆå¤šå¸®åŠ©ï¼Œæˆ‘ä¹Ÿä¸ºä»–å†™è¿‡ä¸€äº›æ–‡ç« ã€‚ å…¶é—´æˆ‘å ‘ä»–è¯‰è¯´äº†å –ä¹¦å  çš„è‹¦æ ¼ã€‚å°½ç®¡æˆ‘çŸ¥é “"é‡‘é’±"ä¸€è¯ ä¸ å¤ªå ˆé€‚ï¼Œ ä½†æˆ‘è¿˜æ˜¯å¯¹ä»–è¯´ï¼Œæˆ‘æ‰“ç®—æŠŠä¹¦å  å®šä¸ºã€Šé‡‘é’±å“²å­¦å®¶ã€‹ï¼ˆThe Money Philosophersï¼‰ã€‚ä»–å¯¹æˆ‘è¯´ï¼š"ä½ çš„æ„ æ€ æ˜¯'ä¸–ä¿—çš„'ï¼ˆworldlyï¼‰ã€‚"æˆ‘ è¯´ï¼š"è¿™é¡¿é¥­æˆ‘è¯·ã€‚" æˆ‘å¯¹ã€Šä¸–ä¿—å“²å­¦å®¶ã€‹è¿™ä¸ªä¹¦å  å¾ˆæ»¡æ„ ï¼Œä½†å‡ºç‰ˆå•†ä¸ è¿™ä¹ˆæƒ³ã€‚è¿™æœ¬ ä¹¦ä¸Šå¸‚å Žä»¤æ‰€æœ‰äººæƒŠè®¶çš„æ˜¯ï¼Œå‡ºç‰ˆå•†å»ºè®®æŠŠä¹¦å  æ”¹ä¸ºã€Šä¼Ÿå¤§çš„ç» æµŽå­¦ å®¶ã€‹ï¼ˆThe Great Economistsï¼‰ã€‚å¹¸å¥½æ²¡è¿™ä¹ˆå šã€‚å ¯èƒ½ä»–ä»¬ä»¥ä¸ºï¼Œäºº.

Analyst reading
For a portfolio manager, the most important use of this PDF is not just the headline call, but the causal chain: what changed in data, how it changes estimates or positioning, and what would falsify the view. When a formal rating or target price appears above, it should be treated as the report's explicit advice. When no rating appears, the relevant advice is thematic: use the data to size exposure, identify second-order beneficiaries, and define stop-loss/watch-list variables around the risks listed above.

Analyst reading
For a portfolio manager, the most important use of this PDF is not just the headline call, but the causal chain: what changed in data, how it changes estimates or positioning, and what would falsify the view. When a formal rating or target price appears above, it should be treated as the report's explicit advice. When no rating appears, the relevant advice is thematic: use the data to size exposure, identify second-order beneficiaries, and define stop-loss/watch-list variables around the risks listed above.
